src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/PIA16711-MarsCuriosityRover-SayunyeiRock-20130122wh.jpg/167px-PIA16711-MarsCuriosityRover-SayunyeiRock-20130122wh.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/PIA16711-MarsCuriosityRover-SayunyeiRock-20130122wh.jpg/251px-PIA16711-MarsCuriosityRover-SayunyeiRock-20130122wh.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/PIA16711-MarsCuriosityRover-SayunyeiRock-20130122wh.jpg/334px-PIA16711-MarsCuriosityRover-SayunyeiRock-20130122wh.jpg 2x" width="167"/></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:169px;max-width:169px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:124px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PIA16712-MarsCuriosityRover-SayuneiRock-20130122uv.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1195" data-file-width="1605" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/PIA16712-MarsCuriosityRover-SayuneiRock-20130122uv.jpg/167px-PIA16712-MarsCuriosityRover-SayuneiRock-20130122uv.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/PIA16712-MarsCuriosityRover-SayuneiRock-20130122uv.jpg/251px-PIA16712-MarsCuriosityRover-SayuneiRock-20130122uv.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/PIA16712-MarsCuriosityRover-SayuneiRock-20130122uv.jpg/334px-PIA16712-MarsCuriosityRover-SayuneiRock-20130122uv.jpg 2x" width="167"/></a></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">First night-time pictures on Mars (white-light left/<a href="/wiki/Ultraviolet" title="Ultraviolet">UV</a> right) (<i>Curiosity</i> viewing <a href="/wiki/List_of_rocks_on_Mars#Curiosity" title="List of rocks on Mars">Sayunei</a> rock, January 22, 2013)</div></div></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sample_Analysis_at_Mars" title="Sample Analysis at Mars">Sample Analysis at Mars</a></div>
<p>The SAM instrument suite analyzes <a href="/wiki/Organic_compound" title="Organic compound">organics</a> and gases from both atmospheric and solid samples. It consists of instruments developed by the NASA <a href="/wiki/Goddard_Space_Flight_Center" title="Goddard Space Flight Center">Goddard Space Flight Center</a>, the Laboratoire Inter-Universitaire des Systèmes Atmosphériques (LISA) (jointly operated by France's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CNRS" title="CNRS">CNRS</a> and Parisian universities), and <a href="/wiki/Honeybee_Robotics" title="Honeybee Robotics">Honeybee Robotics</a>, along with many additional external partners.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MSLSAM_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-MSLSAM-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-search_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-search-102">[102]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAM_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-SAM-103">[103]</a></sup> The three main instruments are a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quadrupole_Mass_Spectrometer" title="Quadrupole Mass Spectrometer">Quadrupole Mass Spectrometer</a> (QMS), a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gas_chromatograph" title="Gas chromatograph">gas chromatograph</a> (GC) and a <a href="/wiki/Resonance_Raman_spectroscopy#Instrumentation" title="Resonance Raman spectroscopy">tunable laser spectrometer (TLS)</a>. These instruments will perform precision measurements of <a href="/wiki/Oxygen" title="Oxygen">oxygen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carbon" title="Carbon">carbon</a> <a href="/wiki/Isotope" title="Isotope">isotope</a> ratios in <a href="/wiki/Atmosphere_of_Mars#Carbon_dioxide" title="Atmosphere of Mars">carbon dioxide</a> (CO<sub>2</sub>) and <a href="/wiki/Atmosphere_of_Mars#Methane" title="Atmosphere of Mars">methane</a> (CH<sub>4</sub>) in the <a href="/wiki/Atmosphere_of_Mars" title="Atmosphere of Mars">atmosphere of Mars</a> in order to distinguish between their <a href="/wiki/Geochemistry" title="Geochemistry">geochemical</a> or <a href="/wiki/Biology" title="Biology">biological</a> origin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MSLSAM_59-2"><a href="#cite_note-MSLSAM-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAM_103-1"><a href="#cite_note-SAM-103">[103]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-astrobio.2765_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-astrobio.2765-104">[104]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-optics.6923_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-optics.6923-105">[105]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mah2012_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mah2012-106">[106]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Dust_Removal_Tool_.28DRT.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Dust_Removal_Tool_(DRT)">Dust Removal Tool (DRT)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Curiosity_(rover)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Dust Removal Tool (DRT)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:342px;max-width:342px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:169px;max-width:169px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:124px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PIA16619-MarsCuriosityRover-Ekwir1-CleanDRT-20130106.gif"><img alt="" data-file-height="882" data-file-width="1182" height="125" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/PIA16619-MarsCuriosityRover-Ekwir1-CleanDRT-20130106.gif/167px-PIA16619-MarsCuriosityRover-Ekwir1-CleanDRT-20130106.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/PIA16619-MarsCuriosityRover-Ekwir1-CleanDRT-20130106.gif/251px-PIA16619-MarsCuriosityRover-Ekwir1-CleanDRT-20130106.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/PIA16619-MarsCuriosityRover-Ekwir1-CleanDRT-20130106.gif/334px-PIA16619-MarsCuriosityRover-Ekwir1-CleanDRT-20130106.gif 2x" width="167"/></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:169px;max-width:169px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:124px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MarsCuriosityRover-DustRemovalTool-Before-PIA16566.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1196" data-file-width="1605" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/MarsCuriosityRover-DustRemovalTool-Before-PIA16566.jpg/167px-MarsCuriosityRover-DustRemovalTool-Before-PIA16566.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/MarsCuriosityRover-DustRemovalTool-Before-PIA16566.jpg/251px-MarsCuriosityRover-DustRemovalTool-Before-PIA16566.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/MarsCuriosityRover-DustRemovalTool-Before-PIA16566.jpg/334px-MarsCuriosityRover-DustRemovalTool-Before-PIA16566.jpg 2x" width="167"/></a></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">First use of <i>Curiosity</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'s</span> <a href="#Dust_Removal_Tool_(DRT)">Dust Removal Tool</a> (DRT) (January 6, 2013); <a href="/wiki/List_of_rocks_on_Mars#Curiosity" title="List of rocks on Mars">Ekwir_1</a> rock before/after cleaning (left) and closeup (right)</div></div></div>
<p>The Dust Removal Tool (DRT) is a motorized, wire-bristle brush on the turret at the end of <i>Curiosity</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'s</span> arm. The DRT was first used on a rock target named <a href="/wiki/List_of_rocks_on_Mars#Curiosity" title="List of rocks on Mars">Ekwir_1</a> on January 6, 2013. <a href="/wiki/Honeybee_Robotics" title="Honeybee Robotics">Honeybee Robotics</a> built the DRT.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-space20130107_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-space20130107-107">[107]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Radiation_assessment_detector_.28RAD.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Radiation_assessment_detector_(RAD)">Radiation assessment detector (RAD)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Curiosity_(rover)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Radiation assessment detector (RAD)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Radiation_assessment_detector" title="Radiation assessment detector">Radiation assessment detector</a></div>
<p>This instrument was the first of ten MSL instruments to be turned on. Its first role was to characterize the broad spectrum of radiation environment found inside the spacecraft during the cruise phase. These measurements have never been done before from the inside of a spacecraft in interplanetary space. Its primary purpose is to determine the viability and shielding needs for potential human explorers, as well as to characterize the radiation environment on the surface of Mars, which it started doing immediately after MSL landed in August 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MSLRAD_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-MSLRAD-108">[108]</a></sup> Funded by the Exploration Systems Mission Directorate at NASA Headquarters and Germany's Space Agency (DLR), RAD was developed by <a href="/wiki/Southwest_Research_Institute" title="Southwest Research Institute">Southwest Research Institute</a> (SwRI) and the extraterrestrial physics group at <a href="/wiki/University_of_Kiel" title="University of Kiel">Christian-Albrechts-Universität zu Kiel</a>, Germany.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MSLRAD_108-1"><a href="#cite_note-MSLRAD-108">[108]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rad_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-rad-109">[109]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Dynamic_Albedo_of_Neutrons_.28DAN.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Dynamic_Albedo_of_Neutrons_(DAN)">Dynamic Albedo of Neutrons (DAN)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Curiosity_(rover)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Dynamic Albedo of Neutrons (DAN)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Dynamic_Albedo_of_Neutrons" title="Dynamic Albedo of Neutrons">Dynamic Albedo of Neutrons</a></div>
<p>A pulsed sealed-tube <a href="/wiki/Neutron_source" title="Neutron source">neutron source</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IKI_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-IKI-110">[110]</a></sup> and detector for measuring <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen" title="Hydrogen">hydrogen</a> or ice and water at or near the Martian surface, provided by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Federal_Space_Agency" title="Russian Federal Space Agency">Russian Federal Space Agency</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MSLDAN_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-MSLDAN-111">[111]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Dynamic_Albedo_of_Neutrons_(DAN)_Experiment_for_NASA's_2009_Mars_Science_Laboratory_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Dynamic_Albedo_of_Neutrons_(DAN)_Experiment_for_NASA's_2009_Mars_Science_Laboratory-112">[112]</a></sup> and funded by Russia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mars_Science_Laboratory:_Mission_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mars_Science_Laboratory:_Mission-113">[113]</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:left;"></div>
<h3><span id="Mars_Descent_Imager_.28MARDI.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Mars_Descent_Imager_(MARDI)">Mars Descent Imager (MARDI)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Curiosity_(rover)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Mars Descent Imager (MARDI)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MARDI-MSL-camera.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="1504" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/MARDI-MSL-camera.jpg/220px-MARDI-MSL-camera.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/MARDI-MSL-camera.jpg/330px-MARDI-MSL-camera.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/MARDI-MSL-camera.jpg/440px-MARDI-MSL-camera.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MARDI-MSL-camera.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>MARDI camera</div></div></div>
<p>MARDI was fixed to the lower front left corner of the body of <i>Curiosity</i>. During the descent to the Martian surface, MARDI took color images at 1600×1200 pixels with a 1.3-millisecond exposure time starting at distances of about 3.7 km (2.3 mi) to near 5 m (16 ft) from the ground, at a rate of four <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frames_per_second" title="Frames per second">frames per second</a> for about two minutes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MARDI_64-1"><a href="#cite_note-MARDI-64">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mars_Descent_Imager_(MARDI)_Update_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mars_Descent_Imager_(MARDI)_Update-114">[114]</a></sup> MARDI has a pixel scale of 1.5 m (4.9 ft) at 2 km (1.2 mi) to 1.5 mm (0.059 in) at 2 m (6.6 ft) and has a 90° circular field of view. MARDI has eight gigabytes of internal buffer memory that is capable of storing over 4,000 raw images. MARDI imaging allowed the mapping of surrounding terrain and the location of landing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MARDI_64-2"><a href="#cite_note-MARDI-64">[64]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/JunoCam" title="JunoCam">JunoCam</a>, built for the <a href="/wiki/Juno_(spacecraft)" title="Juno (spacecraft)">Juno spacecraft</a>, is based on MARDI.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Junocam,_Juno_Jupiter_Orbiter_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-Junocam,_Juno_Jupiter_Orbiter-115">[115]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Robotic_arm">Robotic arm</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Curiosity_(rover)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Robotic arm">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;max-width:192px"><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:190px;max-width:190px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:167px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PIA16225-MarsCuriosityRover-ScooperTest-20121008.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1345" height="168" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/PIA16225-MarsCuriosityRover-ScooperTest-20121008.jpg/188px-PIA16225-MarsCuriosityRover-ScooperTest-20121008.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/PIA16225-MarsCuriosityRover-ScooperTest-20121008.jpg/282px-PIA16225-MarsCuriosityRover-ScooperTest-20121008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/PIA16225-MarsCuriosityRover-ScooperTest-20121008.jpg/376px-PIA16225-MarsCuriosityRover-ScooperTest-20121008.jpg 2x" width="188"/></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:190px;max-width:190px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:74px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PIA16226-MarsCuriosityRover-FirstScoopOfSoil-20121007.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="3020" height="75" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/PIA16226-MarsCuriosityRover-FirstScoopOfSoil-20121007.jpg/188px-PIA16226-MarsCuriosityRover-FirstScoopOfSoil-20121007.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/PIA16226-MarsCuriosityRover-FirstScoopOfSoil-20121007.jpg/282px-PIA16226-MarsCuriosityRover-FirstScoopOfSoil-20121007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/PIA16226-MarsCuriosityRover-FirstScoopOfSoil-20121007.jpg/376px-PIA16226-MarsCuriosityRover-FirstScoopOfSoil-20121007.jpg 2x" width="188"/></a></div></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">First use of <i>Curiosity</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'s</span> <a href="#Robotic_arm">scooper</a> as it sifts a load of <a href="/wiki/Martian_soil" title="Martian soil">sand</a> at <a href="/wiki/Rocknest_(Mars)" title="Rocknest (Mars)">Rocknest</a> (October 7, 2012)</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MarsCuriosityRover-Drilling-01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1200" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/MarsCuriosityRover-Drilling-01.jpg/220px-MarsCuriosityRover-Drilling-01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/MarsCuriosityRover-Drilling-01.jpg/330px-MarsCuriosityRover-Drilling-01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/MarsCuriosityRover-Drilling-01.jpg/440px-MarsCuriosityRover-Drilling-01.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MarsCuriosityRover-Drilling-01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Mars_Science_Laboratory#Images" title="Timeline of Mars Science Laboratory">First drill tests</a> (<a href="/wiki/List_of_rocks_on_Mars#Curiosity" title="List of rocks on Mars">John Klein rock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yellowknife_Bay,_Mars" title="Yellowknife Bay, Mars">Yellowknife Bay</a>, February 2, 2013).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TMJ-20130203_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-TMJ-20130203-116">[116]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>The rover has a 2.1 m (6.9 ft) long <a href="/wiki/Robotic_arm" title="Robotic arm">robotic arm</a> with a cross-shaped turret holding five devices that can spin through a 350° turning range.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rover_arm_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-rover_arm-117">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Test_challenges_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-Test_challenges-118">[118]</a></sup> The arm makes use of three joints to extend it forward and to stow it again while driving. It has a mass of 30 kg (66 lb) and its diameter, including the tools mounted on it, is about 60 cm (24 in).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stretches_arm_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-stretches_arm-119">[119]</a></sup> It was designed, built, and tested by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MacDonald,_Dettwiler_and_Associates" title="MacDonald, Dettwiler and Associates">MDA US Systems</a>, building upon their prior robotic arm work on the <a href="/wiki/Mars_Surveyor_2001_Lander" title="Mars Surveyor 2001 Lander">Mars Surveyor 2001 Lander</a>, the <i><a href="/wiki/Phoenix_(spacecraft)" title="Phoenix (spacecraft)">Phoenix</a></i> lander, and the two <a href="/wiki/Mars_Exploration_Rover" title="Mars Exploration Rover">Mars Exploration Rovers</a>, <i>Spirit</i> and <i>Opportunity</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup>
</p><p>Two of the five devices are <i>in-situ</i> or contact instruments known as the <a href="#Alpha_Particle_X-ray_Spectrometer_(APXS)">X-ray spectrometer</a> (APXS), and the <a href="/wiki/Mars_Hand_Lens_Imager" title="Mars Hand Lens Imager">Mars Hand Lens Imager</a> (MAHLI camera). The remaining three are associated with sample acquisition and sample preparation functions: a <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Mars_Science_Laboratory#Images" title="Timeline of Mars Science Laboratory">percussion drill</a>; a brush; and mechanisms for scooping, sieving, and portioning samples of powdered rock and soil.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rover_arm_117-1"><a href="#cite_note-rover_arm-117">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stretches_arm_119-1"><a href="#cite_note-stretches_arm-119">[119]</a></sup> The diameter of the hole in a rock after drilling is 1.6 cm (0.63 in) and up to 5 cm (2.0 in) deep.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Test_challenges_118-1"><a href="#cite_note-Test_challenges-118">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Washington_U_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-Washington_U-121">[121]</a></sup> The drill carries two spare bits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Washington_U_121-1"><a href="#cite_note-Washington_U-121">[121]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-esmats.2011_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-esmats.2011-122">[122]</a></sup> The rover's arm and turret system can place the APXS and MAHLI on their respective targets, and also obtain powdered sample from rock interiors, and deliver them to the <a href="/wiki/Sample_Analysis_at_Mars" title="Sample Analysis at Mars">SAM</a> and <a href="/wiki/CheMin" title="CheMin">CheMin</a> analyzers inside the rover.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Test_challenges_118-2"><a href="#cite_note-Test_challenges-118">[118]</a></sup>
</p><p>Since early 2015 the percussive mechanism in the drill that helps chisel into rock has had an intermittent electrical short.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-drill-fault_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-drill-fault-123">[123]</a></sup> On December 1, 2016, the motor inside the drill caused a malfunction that prevented the rover from moving its robotic arm and driving to another location.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-popmech20161213_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-popmech20161213-124">[124]</a></sup> The fault was isolated to the drill feed brake,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spacecom20161215_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-spacecom20161215-125">[125]</a></sup> and internal debris is suspected of causing the problem.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-drill-fault_123-1"><a href="#cite_note-drill-fault-123">[123]</a></sup> By December 9, driving and robotic arm operations were cleared to continue, but drilling remained suspended indefinitely.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nasa20161209_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-nasa20161209-126">[126]</a></sup> The <i>Curiosity</i> team continued to perform diagnostics and testing on the drill mechanism throughout 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-planetary20170906_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-planetary20170906-127">[127]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Comparisons_to_other_Mars_missions">Comparisons to other Mars missions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Curiosity_(rover)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Comparisons to other Mars missions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PIA15279_3rovers-stand_D2011_1215_D521.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2889" data-file-width="5723" height="202" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/PIA15279_3rovers-stand_D2011_1215_D521.jpg/400px-PIA15279_3rovers-stand_D2011_1215_D521.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/PIA15279_3rovers-stand_D2011_1215_D521.jpg/600px-PIA15279_3rovers-stand_D2011_1215_D521.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/PIA15279_3rovers-stand_D2011_1215_D521.jpg/800px-PIA15279_3rovers-stand_D2011_1215_D521.jpg 2x" width="400"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PIA15279_3rovers-stand_D2011_1215_D521.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Two Jet Propulsion Laboratory engineers stand with three vehicles, providing a size comparison of three generations of Mars rovers. Front and center is the flight spare for the first Mars rover, <i>Sojourner</i>, which landed on Mars in 1997 as part of the Mars Pathfinder Project. On the left is a Mars Exploration Rover (MER) test vehicle that is a working sibling to <i>Spirit</i> and <i>Opportunity</i>, which landed on Mars in 2004. On the right is a test rover for the Mars Science Laboratory, which landed <i>Curiosity</i> on Mars in 2012.<div class="paragraphbreak" style="margin-top:0.5em"></div> <i>Sojourner</i> is 65 cm (2.13 ft) long. The Mars Exploration Rovers (MER) are 1.6 m (5.2 ft) long. <i>Curiosity</i> on the right is 3 m (9.8 ft) long.</div></div></div>
<p><i>Curiosity</i> has an advanced <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Payload_(air_and_space_craft)" title="Payload (air and space craft)">payload</a> of scientific equipment on Mars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-facts_54-2"><a href="#cite_note-facts-54">[54]</a></sup> It is the fourth NASA unmanned surface rover sent to Mars since 1996. Previous successful Mars rovers are <i><a href="/wiki/Sojourner_(rover)" title="Sojourner (rover)">Sojourner</a></i> from the <a href="/wiki/Mars_Pathfinder" title="Mars Pathfinder">Mars Pathfinder</a> mission (1997), and <i><a href="/wiki/Spirit_(rover)" title="Spirit (rover)">Spirit</a></i> (2004–2010) and <i><a href="/wiki/Opportunity_(rover)" title="Opportunity (rover)">Opportunity</a></i> (2004–present) rovers from the <a href="/wiki/Mars_Exploration_Rover" title="Mars Exploration Rover">Mars Exploration Rover</a> mission.
</p><p><i>Curiosity</i> is 2.9 m (9.5 ft) long by 2.7 m (8.9 ft) wide by 2.2 m (7.2 ft) in height,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnes_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-cnes-24">[24]</a></sup> larger than Mars Exploration Rovers, which are 1.5 m (4.9 ft) long and have a mass of 174 kg (384 lb) including 6.8 kg (15 lb) of scientific instruments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MSLUSAToday_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-MSLUSAToday-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mars_Rovers:_Pathfinder,_MER_(Spirit_and_Opportunity),_and_MSL_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mars_Rovers:_Pathfinder,_MER_(Spirit_and_Opportunity),_and_MSL-128">[128]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mars_Exploration_Rover_Launches_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mars_Exploration_Rover_Launches-129">[129]</a></sup> In comparison to <a href="/wiki/Pancam" title="Pancam">Pancam</a> on the Mars Exploration Rovers, the MastCam-34 has 1.25× higher <a href="/wiki/Angular_resolution" title="Angular resolution">spatial resolution</a> and the MastCam-100 has 3.67× higher spatial resolution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MastCamDescription_65-2"><a href="#cite_note-MastCamDescription-65">[65]</a></sup>
</p><p>The region the rover is set to explore has been compared to the <a href="/wiki/Four_Corners" title="Four Corners">Four Corners</a> region of the North American west.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nasa.pia16068_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-nasa.pia16068-130">[130]</a></sup> Gale Crater has an area similar to <a href="/wiki/Connecticut" title="Connecticut">Connecticut</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island" title="Rhode Island">Rhode Island</a> combined.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nasa.pia15987_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-nasa.pia15987-131">[131]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Colin_Pillinger" title="Colin Pillinger">Colin Pillinger</a>, leader of the <i><a href="/wiki/Beagle_2" title="Beagle 2">Beagle 2</a></i> project, reacted emotionally to a large number of technicians monitoring <i>Curiosity</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'s</span> descent, because <i>Beagle 2</i> had only four people monitoring it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sun_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-sun-132">[132]</a></sup> The <i>Beagle 2</i> team made a virtue out of necessity; it was known that there was no chance of obtaining funds in Europe, at that time, of the scale previously considered necessary for a Mars rover, so the team used innovative methods to reduce the cost to less than 4% of the cost of the <i>Curiosity</i> mission. They also had only one shot, with no funding for repeat missions (it was named <i>Beagle 2</i> as a successor to <a href="/wiki/HMS_Beagle" title="HMS Beagle">HMS <i>Beagle</i></a>, not to an earlier rover).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sun_132-1"><a href="#cite_note-sun-132">[132]</a></sup> It was considered a large risk, and, although <i>Beagle 2</i> did successfully survive its entry, descent, and landing, incomplete deployment of the solar panels hampered communication back to Earth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardian20150117_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-guardian20150117-133">[133]</a></sup> The team has proposed that a future launch might take multiple low-cost <i>Beagle</i>-type landers, with a realistic expectation that the vast majority would be successful, allowing exploration of several parts of Mars and possibly asteroids, all for considerably less cost than a single "normal" rover expedition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gib_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-gib-134">[134]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Comparison_of_embedded_computer_systems_on_board_the_Mars_rovers" title="Comparison of embedded computer systems on board the Mars rovers">Comparison of embedded computer systems on board the Mars rovers</a></div>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="The_name:_Curiosity">The name: <i>Curiosity</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Curiosity_(rover)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: The name: Curiosity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Clara-ma-rover.jpg"><img alt="Clara Ma" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="282" data-file-width="425" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/55/Clara-ma-rover.jpg/220px-Clara-ma-rover.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/55/Clara-ma-rover.jpg/330px-Clara-ma-rover.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/5/55/Clara-ma-rover.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Clara-ma-rover.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Clara Ma, winner of the Mars Science Laboratory naming contest</div></div></div>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> panel selected the name <i>Curiosity</i> following a nationwide student contest that attracted more than 9,000 proposals via the Internet and mail. A sixth-grade student from <a href="/wiki/Kansas" title="Kansas">Kansas</a>, twelve-year-old Clara Ma from Sunflower Elementary School in <a href="/wiki/Lenexa,_Kansas" title="Lenexa, Kansas">Lenexa, Kansas</a>, submitted the winning entry. As her prize, Ma won a trip to <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Jet_Propulsion_Laboratory" title="Jet Propulsion Laboratory">Jet Propulsion Laboratory</a> (JPL) in <a href="/wiki/Pasadena,_California" title="Pasadena, California">Pasadena, California</a>, where she signed her name directly onto the rover as it was being assembled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-NASA-135">[135]</a></sup>
</p><p>Ma wrote in her winning essay:
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303468">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Curiosity is an everlasting flame that burns in everyone's mind. It makes me get out of bed in the morning and wonder what surprises life will throw at me that day. Curiosity is such a powerful force. Without it, we wouldn't be who we are today. Curiosity is the passion that drives us through our everyday lives. We have become explorers and scientists with our need to ask questions and to wonder.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA_135-1"><a href="#cite_note-NASA-135">[135]</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Landing">Landing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Curiosity_(rover)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Landing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Landing_site">Landing site</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Curiosity_(rover)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Landing site">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Bradbury_Landing" title="Bradbury Landing">Bradbury Landing</a></div>
<p><i>Curiosity</i> landed in Quad 51 (nicknamed Yellowknife) of <a href="/wiki/Aeolis_Palus" title="Aeolis Palus">Aeolis Palus</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gale_Crater" title="Gale Crater">Gale Crater</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA-20120810_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-NASA-20120810-136">[136]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA-20120809_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-NASA-20120809-137">[137]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC-20120809_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-20120809-138">[138]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USA-20120809_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-USA-20120809-139">[139]</a></sup> The landing site coordinates are: <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Curiosity_(rover)&amp;params=4.5895_S_137.4417_E_globe:Mars"><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">4°35′22″S</span> <span class="longitude">137°26′30″E</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">﻿ / ﻿</span><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">4.5895°S 137.4417°E</span><span style="display:none">﻿ / <span class="geo">-4.5895; 137.4417</span></span></span></a></span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MSNBC-20120806_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-MSNBC-20120806-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-S&amp;T-20120807_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-S&amp;T-20120807-11">[11]</a></sup> The location has been named <a href="/wiki/Bradbury_Landing" title="Bradbury Landing">Bradbury Landing</a> in honor of science fiction author <a href="/wiki/Ray_Bradbury" title="Ray Bradbury">Ray Bradbury</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA-20120822_9-2"><a href="#cite_note-NASA-20120822-9">[9]</a></sup> Gale crater, an estimated 3.5 to 3.8 billion-year-old impact crater, is hypothesized to have first been gradually filled in by <a href="/wiki/Sediment" title="Sediment">sediments</a>; first water-deposited, and then wind-deposited, possibly until it was completely covered. Wind <a href="/wiki/Erosion" title="Erosion">erosion</a> then scoured out the sediments, leaving an isolated 5.5-kilometer-high (3.4 mi) mountain, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aeolis_Mons" title="Aeolis Mons">Aeolis Mons</a> ("Mount Sharp"), at the center of the 154 km (96 mi) wide crater. Thus, it is believed that the rover may have the opportunity to study two billion years of Martian history in the sediments exposed in the mountain. Additionally, its landing site is near an <a href="/wiki/Alluvial_fan" title="Alluvial fan">alluvial fan</a>, which is hypothesized to be the result of a flow of ground water, either before the deposition of the eroded sediments or else in relatively recent geologic history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Crater_mound_a_prize_and_puzzle_for_Mars_rover_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-Crater_mound_a_prize_and_puzzle_for_Mars_rover-140">[140]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-themis_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-themis-141">[141]</a></sup>
</p><p>According to NASA, an estimated 20,000 to 40,000 heat-resistant <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bacterial_spores" title="Bacterial spores">bacterial spores</a> were on <i>Curiosity</i> at launch, and as much as 1,000 times that number may not have been counted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20151005-kc_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-20151005-kc-142">[142]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width:auto; max-width:1608px;">
<div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PIA16056hl.jpg" title="Curiosity and surrounding area as viewed by MRO/HiRISE. North is left. (August 14, 2012; enhanced colors)"><img alt="" data-file-height="1511" data-file-width="13401" height="180" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/PIA16056hl.jpg/1600px-PIA16056hl.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/PIA16056hl.jpg/2400px-PIA16056hl.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/PIA16056hl.jpg/3200px-PIA16056hl.jpg 2x" width="1600"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="text-align:center"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:PIA16056hl.jpg" title="File:PIA16056hl.jpg"> </a></div><i>Curiosity</i> and surrounding area as viewed by <a href="/wiki/Mars_Reconnaissance_Orbiter" title="Mars Reconnaissance Orbiter">MRO</a>/<a href="/wiki/HiRISE" title="HiRISE">HiRISE</a>. North is left. (August 14, 2012; <a href="/wiki/Mars_surface_color" title="Mars surface color">enhanced colors</a>)</div>
</div></div>
<h3><span id="Rover.27s_role_in_the_landing_system"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Rover's_role_in_the_landing_system">Rover's role in the landing system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Curiosity_(rover)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Rover's role in the landing system">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mars_Science_Laboratory#Entry,_descent,_and_landing_(EDL)" title="Mars Science Laboratory">Mars Science Laboratory–Landing</a></div>

codecs=&amp;quot;vp8, vorbis&amp;quot;" data-title="WebM (360P)" data-shorttitle="WebM 360P" data-transcodekey="360p.webm" data-width="640" data-height="360" data-bandwidth="564200" data-framerate="23.976023976024"/&gt;&lt;/video&gt;&lt;/div&gt;'><img alt="File:Curiosity's Seven Minutes of Terror.ogv" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Curiosity%27s_Seven_Minutes_of_Terror.ogv/220px--Curiosity%27s_Seven_Minutes_of_Terror.ogv.jpg" style="width:220px;height:124px"/><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/96/Curiosity%27s_Seven_Minutes_of_Terror.ogv" target="new" title="Play media"><span class="play-btn-large"><span class="mw-tmh-playtext">Play media</span></span></a></div> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Curiosity%27s_Seven_Minutes_of_Terror.ogv" title="Enlarge"></a></div>NASA video describing the landing procedure. NASA dubbed the landing as "Seven Minutes of Terror".</div></div></div>
<p>Previous NASA <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mars_rovers" title="Mars rovers">Mars rovers</a> became active only after the successful entry, descent, and landing on the Martian surface. <i>Curiosity</i>, on the other hand, was active when it touched down on the surface of Mars, employing the rover suspension system for the final set-down.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnes3_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-cnes3-143">[143]</a></sup>
</p><p><i>Curiosity</i> transformed from its stowed flight configuration to a landing configuration while the MSL spacecraft simultaneously lowered it beneath the spacecraft descent stage with a 20 m (66 ft) tether from the "sky crane" system to a soft landing—wheels down—on the surface of Mars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EntryDescentLanding_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-EntryDescentLanding-144">[144]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sky_Crane_–_how_to_land_Curiosity_on_the_surface_of_Mars_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sky_Crane_–_how_to_land_Curiosity_on_the_surface_of_Mars-145">[145]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mars_rover_lands_on_Xbox_Live_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mars_rover_lands_on_Xbox_Live-146">[146]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mars_Science_Laboratory:_Entry,_Descent,_and_Landing_System_Performance_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mars_Science_Laboratory:_Entry,_Descent,_and_Landing_System_Performance-147">[147]</a></sup> After the rover touched down it waited 2 seconds to confirm that it was on solid ground then fired several <a href="/wiki/Pyrotechnic_fastener" title="Pyrotechnic fastener">pyrotechnic fasteners</a> activating cable cutters on the bridle to free itself from the spacecraft descent stage. The descent stage then flew away to a crash landing, and the rover prepared itself to begin the science portion of the mission.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ellipse_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-ellipse-148">[148]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Coverage.2C_cultural_impact_and_legacy"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Coverage,_cultural_impact_and_legacy">Coverage, cultural impact and legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Curiosity_(rover)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Coverage, cultural impact and legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cheering-full-br2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="570" data-file-width="1024" height="122" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Cheering-full-br2.jpg/220px-Cheering-full-br2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Cheering-full-br2.jpg/330px-Cheering-full-br2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Cheering-full-br2.jpg/440px-Cheering-full-br2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cheering-full-br2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Celebration erupts at NASA with the rover's successful landing on Mars (August 6, 2012).</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:President_Obama_Phones_Mars_Rover_Team.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1365" data-file-width="2048" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/President_Obama_Phones_Mars_Rover_Team.jpg/220px-President_Obama_Phones_Mars_Rover_Team.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/President_Obama_Phones_Mars_Rover_Team.jpg/330px-President_Obama_Phones_Mars_Rover_Team.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/President_Obama_Phones_Mars_Rover_Team.jpg/440px-President_Obama_Phones_Mars_Rover_Team.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:President_Obama_Phones_Mars_Rover_Team.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> congratulates NASA's <i>Curiosity</i> team (August 13, 2012).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20120813_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-20120813-149">[149]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Live video showing the first footage from the surface of Mars was available at <a href="/wiki/NASA_TV" title="NASA TV">NASA TV</a>, during the late hours of August 6, 2012, PDT, including interviews with the mission team. The NASA website momentarily became unavailable from the overwhelming number of people visiting it,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lands_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lands-150">[150]</a></sup> and a 13-minute NASA excerpt of the landings on its YouTube channel was halted an hour after the landing by an automated <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DMCA" title="DMCA">DMCA</a> takedown notice from <a href="/wiki/E._W._Scripps_Company" title="E. W. Scripps Company">Scripps Local News</a>, which prevented access for several hours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vice_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-vice-151">[151]</a></sup> Around 1,000 people gathered in New York City's <a href="/wiki/Times_Square" title="Times Square">Times Square</a>, to watch NASA's live broadcast of <i>Curiosity</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'s</span> landing, as footage was being shown on the giant screen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TimeSquare_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-TimeSquare-152">[152]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bobak_Ferdowsi" title="Bobak Ferdowsi">Bobak Ferdowsi</a>, Flight Director for the landing, became an <a href="/wiki/Internet_meme" title="Internet meme">Internet meme</a> and attained Twitter celebrity status, with 45,000 new followers subscribing to his Twitter account, due to his <a href="/wiki/Mohawk_hairstyle" title="Mohawk hairstyle">Mohawk hairstyle</a> with yellow stars that he wore during the televised broadcast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-space_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-space-153">[153]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VentureBeat_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-VentureBeat-154">[154]</a></sup>
</p><p>On August 13, 2012, U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>, calling from aboard <a href="/wiki/Air_Force_One" title="Air Force One">Air Force One</a> to congratulate the <i>Curiosity</i> team, said, "You guys are examples of American know-how and ingenuity. It's really an amazing accomplishment."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20120813_149-1"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-20120813-149">[149]</a></sup> (<a class="external text" href="http://mars.jpl.nasa.gov/multimedia/videos/movies/msl20120813_obamacall/msl20120813_obamacall-320.mov" rel="nofollow">Video (07:20)</a>)
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:342px;max-width:342px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:185px;max-width:185px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:137px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PIA15882-Mars_Curiosity_Rover-USA-Flag.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1184" data-file-width="1584" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/PIA15882-Mars_Curiosity_Rover-USA-Flag.jpg/183px-PIA15882-Mars_Curiosity_Rover-USA-Flag.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/PIA15882-Mars_Curiosity_Rover-USA-Flag.jpg/275px-PIA15882-Mars_Curiosity_Rover-USA-Flag.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/PIA15882-Mars_Curiosity_Rover-USA-Flag.jpg/366px-PIA15882-Mars_Curiosity_Rover-USA-Flag.jpg 2x" width="183"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">U.S. flag on Mars</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:153px;max-width:153px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:137px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PIA15883-Mars_Curiosity_Rover-President_Obama_Signature_on_Plaque.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="2199" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/PIA15883-Mars_Curiosity_Rover-President_Obama_Signature_on_Plaque.jpg/151px-PIA15883-Mars_Curiosity_Rover-President_Obama_Signature_on_Plaque.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/PIA15883-Mars_Curiosity_Rover-President_Obama_Signature_on_Plaque.jpg/227px-PIA15883-Mars_Curiosity_Rover-President_Obama_Signature_on_Plaque.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/PIA15883-Mars_Curiosity_Rover-President_Obama_Signature_on_Plaque.jpg/302px-PIA15883-Mars_Curiosity_Rover-President_Obama_Signature_on_Plaque.jpg 2x" width="151"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Commemorative_plaque" title="Commemorative plaque">Plaque</a> of <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">President Obama</a> and Vice President <a href="/wiki/Joe_Biden" title="Joe Biden">Joe Biden</a>'s signatures on Mars</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>
<p>Scientists at the <a href="/wiki/Getty_Conservation_Institute" title="Getty Conservation Institute">Getty Conservation Institute</a> in Los Angeles, California, viewed the CheMin instrument aboard <i>Curiosity</i> as a potentially valuable means to examine ancient works of art without damaging them. Until recently, only a few instruments were available to determine the composition without cutting out physical samples large enough to potentially damage the artifacts. CheMin directs a beam of <a href="/wiki/X-ray" title="X-ray">X-rays</a> at particles as small as 400 micrometers (0.016 in)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-inxitu_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-inxitu-155">[155]</a></sup> and reads the <a href="/wiki/Radiation" title="Radiation">radiation</a> <a href="/wiki/Scattering" title="Scattering">scattered</a> back to determine the composition of the artifact in minutes. Engineers created a smaller, portable version named the <i>X-Duetto</i>. Fitting into a few <a href="/wiki/Briefcase" title="Briefcase">briefcase</a>-sized boxes, it can examine objects on site, while preserving their physical integrity. It is now being used by Getty scientists to analyze a large collection of the museum <a href="/wiki/Antique" title="Antique">antiques</a> and the Roman ruins of <a href="/wiki/Herculaneum" title="Herculaneum">Herculaneum</a>, Italy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NS-201208_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-NS-201208-156">[156]</a></sup>
</p><p>Prior to the landing, NASA and <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a> released <i>Mars Rover Landing</i>, a free downloadable game on <a href="/wiki/Xbox_Live" title="Xbox Live">Xbox Live</a> that uses <a href="/wiki/Kinect" title="Kinect">Kinect</a> to capture body motions, which allows users to simulate the landing sequence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newsday_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-newsday-157">[157]</a></sup>
</p><p>NASA gave the general public the opportunity from 2009 until 2011 to submit their names to be sent to Mars. More than 1.2 million people from the international community participated, and their names were etched into <a href="/wiki/Silicon" title="Silicon">silicon</a> using an electron-beam machine used for fabricating micro devices at <a href="/wiki/Jet_Propulsion_Laboratory" title="Jet Propulsion Laboratory">JPL</a>, and this plaque is now installed on the deck of <i>Curiosity</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Send_Your_Name_to_Mars_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-Send_Your_Name_to_Mars-158">[158]</a></sup> In keeping with a 40-year tradition, a plaque with the signatures of President Barack Obama and <a href="/wiki/Joe_Biden" title="Joe Biden">Vice President Joe Biden</a> was also installed. Elsewhere on the rover is the <a href="/wiki/Autograph" title="Autograph">autograph</a> of Clara Ma, the 12-year-old girl from <a href="/wiki/Kansas" title="Kansas">Kansas</a> who gave <i>Curiosity</i> its name in an essay contest, writing in part that "curiosity is the passion that drives us through our everyday lives."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-collect_159-0"><a href="#cite_note-collect-159">[159]</a></sup>
</p><p>On August 6, 2013, <i>Curiosity</i> audibly played "<a href="/wiki/Happy_Birthday_to_You" title="Happy Birthday to You">Happy Birthday to You</a>" in honor of the one Earth year mark of its Martian landing, the first time for a song to be played on another planet. This was also the first time music was transmitted between two planets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WP-20130806_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-WP-20130806-160">[160]</a></sup>
</p><p>On June 24, 2014, <i>Curiosity</i> completed a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Martian_year" title="Martian year">Martian year</a>—687 Earth days—after finding that Mars once had <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Mars_Science_Laboratory#Evidence_for_ancient_habitability" title="Timeline of Mars Science Laboratory">environmental conditions favorable for microbial life</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA-20140623_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-NASA-20140623-161">[161]</a></sup> <i>Curiosity</i> will serve as the basis for the design of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mars_2020_rover_mission" title="Mars 2020 rover mission">Mars 2020 rover mission</a> that is presently planned to be launched to Mars in 2020. Some spare parts from the build and ground test of <i>Curiosity</i> may be used in the new vehicle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNET_Harwood_first_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-CNET_Harwood_first-162">[162]</a></sup>
</p><p>On August 5, 2017, NASA celebrated the fifth anniversary of the <i>Curiosity</i> rover mission landing, and related exploratory accomplishments, on the planet <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">Mars</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA-20170802_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-NASA-20170802-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SP-20170805_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-SP-20170805-19">[19]</a></sup> (Videos: <a class="external text" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=IxvODcuFb1s" rel="nofollow"><i>Curiosity</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'s</span> First Five Years (02:07)</a>; <a class="external text" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=O0nPFaBU98k" rel="nofollow"><i>Curiosity</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'s</span> POV: Five Years Driving (05:49)</a>; <a class="external text" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Q-uAz82sH-E" rel="nofollow"><i>Curiosity</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'s</span> Discoveries About Gale Crater (02:54)</a>)
</p><p>As reported in 2018, drill samples taken in 2015 uncovered organic molecules of <a href="/wiki/Benzene" title="Benzene">benzene</a> and <a href="/wiki/Propane" title="Propane">propane</a> in 3 billion year old rock samples in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gale_Crater" title="Gale Crater">Gale Crater</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20180607_163-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-20180607-163">[163]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SCI-20180608a_164-0"><a href="#cite_note-SCI-20180608a-164">[164]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SCI-20180608c_165-0"><a href="#cite_note-SCI-20180608c-165">[165]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Mars_Science_Laboratory#Current_status" title="Timeline of Mars Science Laboratory">Timeline of Mars Science Laboratory § Current status</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards">Awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Curiosity_(rover)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Awards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The NASA/JPL <a href="/wiki/Mars_Science_Laboratory" title="Mars Science Laboratory">Mars Science Laboratory</a>/<i>Curiosity</i> Project Team was awarded the 2012 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Robert_J._Collier_Trophy" title="Robert J. Collier Trophy">Robert J. Collier Trophy</a> by the <a href="/wiki/National_Aeronautic_Association" title="National Aeronautic Association">National Aeronautic Association</a> "In recognition of the extraordinary achievements of successfully landing <i>Curiosity</i> on Mars, advancing the nation's technological and engineering capabilities, and significantly improving humanity's understanding of ancient Martian habitable environments."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NAA-20130312_166-0"><a href="#cite_note-NAA-20130312-166">[166]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Images">Images</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Curiosity_(rover)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Images">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Components_of_Curiosity">Components of <i>Curiosity</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Curiosity_(rover)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Components of Curiosity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:15px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:20110406_PIA13809_D2011_0404_D036_cropped-full.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1571" data-file-width="1290" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/20110406_PIA13809_D2011_0404_D036_cropped-full.jpg/98px-20110406_PIA13809_D2011_0404_D036_cropped-full.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/20110406_PIA13809_D2011_0404_D036_cropped-full.jpg/148px-20110406_PIA13809_D2011_0404_D036_cropped-full.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/20110406_PIA13809_D2011_0404_D036_cropped-full.jpg/197px-20110406_PIA13809_D2011_0404_D036_cropped-full.jpg 2x" width="98"/></a></div></div>

<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:45.5px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Curiosity%27s_high_gain_antenna_and_low_gain_antenna.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="454" data-file-width="926" height="59" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Curiosity%27s_high_gain_antenna_and_low_gain_antenna.jpg/120px-Curiosity%27s_high_gain_antenna_and_low_gain_antenna.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Curiosity%27s_high_gain_antenna_and_low_gain_antenna.jpg/180px-Curiosity%27s_high_gain_antenna_and_low_gain_antenna.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Curiosity%27s_high_gain_antenna_and_low_gain_antenna.jpg/240px-Curiosity%27s_high_gain_antenna_and_low_gain_antenna.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a></div></div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p>High-gain (right) and low-gain (left) antennas
</p>
</div>
</div></li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">

title="Image map">Interactive imagemap</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Mars" title="Geography of Mars">global topography of Mars</a>, overlain with <a href="/wiki/List_of_artificial_objects_on_Mars" title="List of artificial objects on Mars">locations of Mars landers and rovers</a> (Red label = <a href="/wiki/Mars_rover" title="Mars rover">Rover</a>; Blue label = <a href="/wiki/Mars_landing" title="Mars landing">Lander</a>; bold red/blue = currently active). Hover your mouse to see the names of over 25 <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Mars" title="Geography of Mars">prominent geographic features</a>, and click to link to them. Coloring of the base map indicates relative <a href="/wiki/Elevation" title="Elevation">elevations</a>, based on data from the <a href="/wiki/Mars_Orbiter_Laser_Altimeter" title="Mars Orbiter Laser Altimeter">Mars Orbiter Laser Altimeter</a> on NASA's <a href="/wiki/Mars_Global_Surveyor" title="Mars Global Surveyor">Mars Global Surveyor</a>. Reds and pinks are higher elevation (+3 km to +8 km); yellow is 0 km; greens and blues are lower elevation (down to −8 km). Whites (&gt;+12 km) and browns (&gt;+8 km) are the highest elevations. <a href="/wiki/Cartesian_coordinate_system" title="Cartesian coordinate system">Axes</a> are <a href="/wiki/Latitude" title="Latitude">latitude</a> and <a href="/wiki/Longitude" title="Longitude">longitude</a>; <a href="/wiki/Geographical_pole" title="Geographical pole">Poles</a> are not shown. <div style="float: right;"><span style="font-size:85%;">(See also: <i><a href="/wiki/Template:Mars_map" title="Template:Mars map">Mars map</a></i> &amp; <i><a href="/wiki/List_of_artificial_objects_on_Mars#Landing_site_namings_and_memorials" title="List of artificial objects on Mars">Mars Memorials</a></i> &amp; <i><a href="/wiki/Template:Features_and_memorials_on_Mars" title="Template:Features and memorials on Mars">Mars Memorials map</a></i>)  (<a href="/wiki/Template:Features_and_artificial_objects_on_Mars" title="Template:Features and artificial objects on Mars">view</a> • <a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Features_and_artificial_objects_on_Mars" title="Template talk:Features and artificial objects on Mars">discuss</a>)</span></div></div></div></div>
